<p><b>Black people</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Human_skin_color" title="Human skin color">skin group</a>-based classification used for specific people with a mid to dark brown <a href="/wiki/Complexion" title="Complexion">complexion</a>. Not all black people have dark skin; however, in certain countries, often in socially based systems of <a href="/wiki/Racial_classification" class="mw-redirect" title="Racial classification">racial classification</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western World</a>, the term <i>black</i> is used to describe persons who are perceived as <a href="/wiki/Dark_skin" title="Dark skin">dark-skinned</a> compared to other populations. It is mostly used for the people of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan African</a> descent and the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> of <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>.
</p><p>Different societies apply different criteria regarding who is classified "black", and these <a href="/wiki/Social_construction" class="mw-redirect" title="Social construction">social constructs</a> have changed over time. In a number of countries, societal variables affect classification as much as skin color, and the social criteria for "blackness" vary. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, "black" was historically equivalent with "<a href="/wiki/Person_of_color" title="Person of color">person of color</a>", a general term for non-European peoples. In other regions such as <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a>, settlers applied the term "black" or it was used by local populations with different histories and ancestral backgrounds.
</p><p>For many other individuals, communities and countries, "black" is also perceived as a derogatory, outdated, reductive or otherwise unrepresentative label, and as a result is neither used nor defined, especially in African cultures with little to no colonial history. Some have pointed out that labeling people groups "black" is erroneous as the people described as  "black" have a brown skin color.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Africa" title="Indigenous peoples of Africa">Indigenous peoples of Africa</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Africa">Northern Africa</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:African_slave_trade.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/African_slave_trade.png/250px-African_slave_trade.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/African_slave_trade.png/375px-African_slave_trade.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/African_slave_trade.png/500px-African_slave_trade.png 2x" data-file-width="721" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:African_slave_trade.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">slave routes</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Africa">Northern Africa</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> interacted with and later conquered parts of <a href="/wiki/Mauretania" title="Mauretania">Mauretania</a>, an early state that covered modern <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, western <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, and the Spanish cities <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> during <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical period</a>. The people of the region were noted in <a href="/wiki/Classical_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical literature">classical literature</a> as <i><a href="/wiki/Mauri_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauri (people)">Mauri</a></i>, which was subsequently rendered as <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a> in English.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Numerous communities of dark-skinned peoples are present in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, some dating from prehistoric communities. Others descend from immigrants via the historical <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">trans-Saharan trade</a> or, after the Arab invasions of North Africa in the 7th century, from slaves from the <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">Arab slave trade</a> in North Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-biomedcentral.com_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biomedcentral.com-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Vrouwen_van_een_Ahwash-dansgroep_uit_de_Anti-Atlas_tijdens_het_nationaal_folklore_festival_te_Marrakech_TMnr_20017645.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Vrouwen_van_een_Ahwash-dansgroep_uit_de_Anti-Atlas_tijdens_het_nationaal_folklore_festival_te_Marrakech_TMnr_20017645.jpg/250px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Vrouwen_van_een_Ahwash-dansgroep_uit_de_Anti-Atlas_tijdens_het_nationaal_folklore_festival_te_Marrakech_TMnr_20017645.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Vrouwen_van_een_Ahwash-dansgroep_uit_de_Anti-Atlas_tijdens_het_nationaal_folklore_festival_te_Marrakech_TMnr_20017645.jpg/375px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Vrouwen_van_een_Ahwash-dansgroep_uit_de_Anti-Atlas_tijdens_het_nationaal_folklore_festival_te_Marrakech_TMnr_20017645.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Vrouwen_van_een_Ahwash-dansgroep_uit_de_Anti-Atlas_tijdens_het_nationaal_folklore_festival_te_Marrakech_TMnr_20017645.jpg/500px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Vrouwen_van_een_Ahwash-dansgroep_uit_de_Anti-Atlas_tijdens_het_nationaal_folklore_festival_te_Marrakech_TMnr_20017645.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Vrouwen_van_een_Ahwash-dansgroep_uit_de_Anti-Atlas_tijdens_het_nationaal_folklore_festival_te_Marrakech_TMnr_20017645.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Haratin" title="Haratin">Haratin</a> women, a community of recent <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan African</a> origin residing in the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In the 18th century, the Moroccan Sultan <a href="/wiki/Moulay_Ismail" class="mw-redirect" title="Moulay Ismail">Moulay Ismail</a> "the Warrior King" (1672–1727) raised a corps of 150,000 black soldiers, called his <a href="/wiki/Black_Guard" title="Black Guard">Black Guard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Moore_(writer)" title="Carlos Moore (writer)">Carlos Moore</a>, resident scholar at Brazil's University of the State of Bahia, in the 21st century Afro-multiracials in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>, including Arabs in North Africa, self-identify in ways that resemble multi-racials in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>. He claims that darker toned Arabs, much like darker toned <a href="/wiki/Latin_Americans" title="Latin Americans">Latin Americans</a>, consider themselves <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white</a> because they have some distant white ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Egyptian President <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">Anwar Sadat</a> had a mother who was a dark-skinned <a href="/wiki/Nubians" title="Nubians">Nubian</a> <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudanese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sudanese_Arabs" title="Sudanese Arabs">Sudanese Arab</a>) woman and a father who was a lighter-skinned <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptian</a>. In response to an advertisement for an acting position, as a young man he said, "I am not white but I am not exactly black either. My blackness is tending to reddish".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/Patriarchy" title="Patriarchy">patriarchal</a> nature of Arab society, Arab men, including during the slave trade in North Africa, enslaved more African women than men. They used more enslaved African female in domestic service and agriculture than males. The men interpreted the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a> to permit sexual relations between a male master and his enslaved females outside of marriage (see <a href="/wiki/Ma_malakat_aymanukum_and_sex" class="mw-redirect" title="Ma malakat aymanukum and sex">Ma malakat aymanukum and sex</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> leading to many <a href="/wiki/Mixed-race" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed-race">mixed-race</a> children. When an enslaved woman became pregnant with her Arab master's child, she was considered as <i><a href="/wiki/Umm_walad" title="Umm walad">umm walad</a></i> or "mother of a child", a status that granted her privileged rights. The child was given rights of inheritance to the father's property, so mixed-race children could share in any wealth of the father.<sup id="cite_ref-hunwick_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hunwick-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Because the society was <a href="/wiki/Patrilineal" class="mw-redirect" title="Patrilineal">patrilineal</a>, the children took their fathers' social status at birth and were born free.
</p><p>Some succeeded their fathers as rulers, such as Sultan <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_al-Mansur" title="Ahmad al-Mansur">Ahmad al-Mansur</a>, who ruled <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> from 1578 to 1608. He was not technically considered as a mixed-race child of a slave; his mother was <a href="/wiki/Fulani" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulani">Fulani</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Concubine" class="mw-redirect" title="Concubine">concubine</a> of his father.<sup id="cite_ref-hunwick_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hunwick-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 1991, non-Arabs of the <a href="/wiki/Zaghawa_people" title="Zaghawa people">Zaghawa people</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> attested that they were victims of an intensifying Arab <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> campaign, segregating Arabs and non-Arabs (specifically, people of <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_peoples" title="Nilotic peoples">Nilotic</a> ancestry).<sup id="cite_ref-Johnson2011_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnson2011-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Sudanese Arabs, who controlled the government, were widely referred to as practicing apartheid against Sudan's non-Arab citizens. The government was accused of "deftly manipulat(ing) Arab solidarity" to carry out policies of apartheid and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lasaga_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lasaga-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/American_University" title="American University">American University</a> economist <a href="/wiki/George_Ayittey" title="George Ayittey">George Ayittey</a> accused the Arab government of Sudan of practicing acts of racism against black citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> According to Ayittey, "In Sudan... the Arabs monopolized power and excluded blacks – Arab apartheid."<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Many African commentators joined Ayittey in accusing Sudan of practising Arab apartheid.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sahara">Sahara</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Bella_vrouw_nabij_Gorom-Gorom_TMnr_20010124.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Bella_vrouw_nabij_Gorom-Gorom_TMnr_20010124.jpg/170px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Bella_vrouw_nabij_Gorom-Gorom_TMnr_20010124.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Bella_vrouw_nabij_Gorom-Gorom_TMnr_20010124.jpg/255px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Bella_vrouw_nabij_Gorom-Gorom_TMnr_20010124.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Bella_vrouw_nabij_Gorom-Gorom_TMnr_20010124.jpg/340px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Bella_vrouw_nabij_Gorom-Gorom_TMnr_20010124.jpg 2x" data-file-width="487" data-file-height="700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Bella_vrouw_nabij_Gorom-Gorom_TMnr_20010124.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Ikelan" title="Ikelan">Ibenheren</a> (Bella) woman</div></div></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>, the native <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berber</a> populations kept "<a href="/wiki/Negro" title="Negro">negro</a>" slaves. Most of these captives were of <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_peoples" title="Nilotic peoples">Nilotic</a> extraction, and were either purchased by the Tuareg nobles from slave markets in the <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(region)" title="Sudan (region)">Western Sudan</a> or taken during raids. Their origin is denoted via the <a href="/wiki/Tamahaq_language" title="Tamahaq language">Ahaggar Berber</a> word <i><a href="/wiki/Ikelan" title="Ikelan">Ibenheren</a></i> (sing. <i>Ébenher</i>), which alludes to slaves that only speak a <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">Nilo-Saharan</a> language. These slaves were also sometimes known by the borrowed <a href="/wiki/Songhay_languages" title="Songhay languages">Songhay</a> term <i>Bella</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">Sahrawi</a> indigenous peoples of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> observed a class system consisting of high <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">castes</a> and low castes. Outside of these traditional tribal boundaries were "Negro" slaves, who were drawn from the surrounding areas.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Horn_of_Africa">Horn of Africa</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_peoples" title="Cushitic peoples">Cushitic peoples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_peoples" title="Nilotic peoples">Nilotic peoples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Habesha_peoples" title="Habesha peoples">Habesha peoples</a></div>
<p>In parts of the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>, the local <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> speaking populations have long adhered to a construct similar to that of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, the slave classes mainly consisted of individuals of Nilotic and <a href="/wiki/Bantus_(Somalia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantus (Somalia)">Bantu</a> origin who were collectively known as <i><a href="/wiki/Shanqella" title="Shanqella">Shanqella</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Adone</i> (both denoting "negro").<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> These captives and others of analogous morphology were distinguished as <i>tsalim barya</i> (dark-skinned slave) in contrast with the Afroasiatic-speaking nobles or <i>saba qayh</i> ("red men") or light-skinned people.<sup id="cite_ref-Tibe_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tibe-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The earliest representation of this tradition dates from a seventh or eighth century BC inscription belonging to the <a href="/wiki/D%CA%BFmt" title="Dʿmt">Kingdom of Damat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_Africa">Southern Africa</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples_in_South_Africa" title="Bantu peoples in South Africa">Bantu peoples in South Africa</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, the period of colonization resulted in many unions and marriages between <a href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="European ethnic groups">European</a> men and <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khoisan" title="Khoisan">Khoisan</a> women from various tribes, resulting in mixed-race children. As the European settlers acquired control of territory, they generally pushed the mixed-race and Bantu and Khoisan populations into second-class status. During the first half of the 20th century, the Afrikaaner-dominated government classified the population according to four main racial groups: <i>Black</i>, <i>White</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a></i> (mostly <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a>), and <i><a href="/wiki/Coloureds" title="Coloureds">Coloured</a></i>. The Coloured group included people of mixed Bantu, Khoisan, and European descent (with some <a href="/wiki/Cape_Malays" title="Cape Malays">Malay</a> ancestry, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Cape" title="Western Cape">Western Cape</a>). The Coloured definition occupied an intermediary political position between the Black and White definitions in South Africa. It imposed a system of legal racial segregation, a complex of laws known as <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Africa_in_the_apartheid_era" class="mw-redirect" title="History of South Africa in the apartheid era">apartheid</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> bureaucracy devised complex (and often arbitrary) criteria in the <a href="/wiki/Population_Registration_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Population Registration Act">Population Registration Act</a> of 1945 to determine who belonged in which group. Minor officials administered tests to enforce the classifications. When it was unclear from a person's physical appearance whether the individual should be considered Coloured or Black, the "<a href="/wiki/Pencil_test_(South_Africa)" title="Pencil test (South Africa)">pencil test</a>" was used. A pencil was inserted into a person's hair to determine if the hair was kinky enough to hold the pencil, rather than having it pass through, as it would with smoother hair. If so, the person was classified as Black.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Such classifications sometimes divided families.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sandra_Laing" title="Sandra Laing">Sandra Laing</a> is a South African woman who was classified as Coloured by authorities during the apartheid era, due to her <a href="/wiki/Human_skin_colour" class="mw-redirect" title="Human skin colour">skin colour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hair#hair_texture" title="Hair">hair texture</a>, although her parents could prove at least three generations of European ancestors. At age 10, she was expelled from her all-white school. The officials' decisions based on her anomalous appearance disrupted her family and adult life. She was the subject of the 2008 biographical dramatic film <i><a href="/wiki/Skin_(2008_film)" title="Skin (2008 film)">Skin</a></i>, which won numerous awards. During the apartheid era, those classed as "Coloured" were oppressed and discriminated against. But, they had limited rights and overall had slightly better socioeconomic conditions than those classed as "Black". The government required that Blacks and Coloureds live in areas separate from Whites, creating large townships located away from the cities as areas for Blacks.
</p><p>In the post-apartheid era, the Constitution of South Africa has declared the country to be a "Non-racial democracy". In an effort to redress past injustices, the ANC government has introduced laws in support of <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a> policies for Blacks; under these they define "Black" people to include "Africans", "Coloureds" and "Asians". Some <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a> policies favor "Africans" over "Coloureds" in terms of qualifying for certain benefits. Some South Africans categorized as "African Black" say that "Coloureds" did not suffer as much as they did during apartheid. "Coloured" South Africans are known to discuss their dilemma by saying, "we were not white enough under apartheid, and we are not black enough under the ANC (<a href="/wiki/African_National_Congress" title="African National Congress">African National Congress</a>)".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, the High Court in South Africa ruled that <a href="/wiki/Chinese_South_Africans" title="Chinese South Africans">Chinese South Africans</a> who were residents during the apartheid era (and their descendants) are to be reclassified as "Black people," solely for the purposes of accessing affirmative action benefits, because they were also "disadvantaged" by racial discrimination. Chinese people who arrived in the country after the end of apartheid do not qualify for such benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other than by appearance, "Coloureds" can usually be distinguished from "Blacks" by language. Most speak <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> or English as a <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a>, as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu languages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> or <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a>. They also tend to have more European-sounding names than <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> names.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Asians" title="Afro-Asians">Afro-Asians</a></div>
<p>"Afro-Asians" or "African-Asians" (also known as "Black Asians" or "Blasian"), are persons of mixed <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_groups_of_Africa" title="List of ethnic groups of Africa">African</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a> ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Historically, Afro-Asian populations have been marginalized as a result of human migration and social conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The term "Black Asian" may also be used to describe <a href="/wiki/Negrito" title="Negrito">Negritos</a> (blacks indigenous to Asia); therefore "Afro-Asian" is a more scientifically proper term to describe Black Asians with direct African background or ancestry.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Asia">Western Asia</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arab_world">Arab world</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Arab" title="Afro-Arab">Afro-Arab</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Bilal.jpg/170px-Bilal.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Bilal.jpg/255px-Bilal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Bilal.jpg/340px-Bilal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="431" data-file-height="718" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bilal_ibn_Ribah" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilal ibn Ribah">Bilal ibn Ribah</a> (<i>pictured</i> atop the <a href="/wiki/Kaaba" title="Kaaba">Kaaba</a>, Mecca) was a former Ethiopian slave and the first <a href="/wiki/Muezzin" class="mw-redirect" title="Muezzin">muezzin</a>, ca. 630.</div></div></div>
<p>Historians estimate that between the advent of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> in 650 CE and the abolition of slavery in the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> in the mid-20th century,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> 10 to 18 million Black Africans (known as the <a href="/wiki/Zanj" title="Zanj">Zanj</a>) were enslaved by Arab slave traders and transported to the Arabian Peninsula and neighboring countries.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> This number far exceeded the number of slaves who were taken to the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Several factors affected the visibility of descendants of this diaspora in 21st-century Arab societies: The traders shipped more female slaves than males, as there was a demand for them to serve as <a href="/wiki/Concubines" class="mw-redirect" title="Concubines">concubines</a> in harems in the Arabian Peninsula and neighboring countries. Male slaves were castrated in order to serve as harem guards. The death toll of Black African slaves from forced labor was high. The mixed-race children of female slaves and Arab owners were assimilated into the Arab owners' families under the <a href="/wiki/Patrilineal" class="mw-redirect" title="Patrilineal">patrilineal</a> <a href="/wiki/Kinship_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Kinship system">kinship system</a>. As a result, few distinctive Afro-Arab communities have survived in the Arabian Peninsula and neighboring countries.<sup id="cite_ref-hidden_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hidden-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Distinctive and self-identified black communities have been reported in countries such as Iraq, with a reported 1.2 million black people, and they attest to a history of discrimination. These descendants of the Zanj have sought minority status from the government, which would reserve some seats in Parliament for representatives of their population.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> According to Alamin M. Mazrui et al., generally in the Arabian Peninsula and neighboring countries, most of these communities identify as both black and Arab.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Iranians" title="Afro-Iranians">Afro-Iranians</a></div>
<p>Afro-Iranians are people of black African ancestry residing in Iran. During the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar dynasty</a>, many wealthy households imported black African women and children as slaves to perform domestic work. This slave labor was drawn exclusively from the <a href="/wiki/Zanj" title="Zanj">Zanj</a>, who were <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>-speaking peoples that lived along the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a>, in an area roughly comprising modern-day <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bagley_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bagley-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ogot_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ogot-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Beta_Israel" title="Beta Israel">Beta Israel</a></div><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/African_Hebrew_Israelites_of_Jerusalem" title="African Hebrew Israelites of Jerusalem">African Hebrew Israelites of Jerusalem</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Israeli_Border_Guard_Police.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Israeli_Border_Guard_Police.jpg/170px-Israeli_Border_Guard_Police.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Israeli_Border_Guard_Police.jpg/255px-Israeli_Border_Guard_Police.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Israeli_Border_Guard_Police.jpg/340px-Israeli_Border_Guard_Police.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="1123" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Israeli_Border_Guard_Police.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">ethnic Jewish</a> (<a href="/wiki/Beta_Israel" title="Beta Israel">Beta Israel</a> Ethiopian Jew) <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> <a href="/wiki/Israel_Border_Police" title="Israel Border Police">Border Policeman</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Black_hebrews_Dimona_children.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Black_hebrews_Dimona_children.jpg/170px-Black_hebrews_Dimona_children.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Black_hebrews_Dimona_children.jpg/255px-Black_hebrews_Dimona_children.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Black_hebrews_Dimona_children.jpg/340px-Black_hebrews_Dimona_children.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Black_hebrews_Dimona_children.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/African_Hebrew_Israelites_of_Jerusalem" title="African Hebrew Israelites of Jerusalem">African Hebrew Israelite</a> child in <a href="/wiki/Dimona" title="Dimona">Dimona</a></div></div></div>
<p>About 150,000 East African and black people live in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, amounting to just over 2% of the nation's population. The vast majority of these, some 120,000, are <a href="/wiki/Beta_Israel" title="Beta Israel">Beta Israel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> most of whom are recent immigrants who came during the 1980s and 1990s from <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Israel is home to over 5,000 members of the <a href="/wiki/African_Hebrew_Israelites_of_Jerusalem" title="African Hebrew Israelites of Jerusalem">African Hebrew Israelites of Jerusalem</a> movement that are ancestry of <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African Americans</a> who emigrated to Israel in the 20th century, and who reside mainly in a distinct neighborhood in the <a href="/wiki/Negev" title="Negev">Negev</a> town of <a href="/wiki/Dimona" title="Dimona">Dimona</a>. Unknown numbers of black converts to Judaism reside in Israel, most of them converts from the United Kingdom, Canada, and the United States.
</p><p>Additionally, there are around 60,000 non-Jewish African immigrants in Israel, some of whom have sought asylum. Most of the migrants are from communities in <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Niger-Congo_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Niger-Congo languages">Niger-Congo</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Nuba_peoples" title="Nuba peoples">Nuba</a> groups of the southern <a href="/wiki/Nuba_Mountains" title="Nuba Mountains">Nuba Mountains</a>; some are illegal immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Turks" title="Afro-Turks">Afro-Turks</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me-Black_Bashi-Bazouk-c._1869.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me-Black_Bashi-Bazouk-c._1869.jpg/220px-G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me-Black_Bashi-Bazouk-c._1869.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me-Black_Bashi-Bazouk-c._1869.jpg/330px-G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me-Black_Bashi-Bazouk-c._1869.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me-Black_Bashi-Bazouk-c._1869.jpg/440px-G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me-Black_Bashi-Bazouk-c._1869.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3147" data-file-height="3896" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me-Black_Bashi-Bazouk-c._1869.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bashi-bazouk" title="Bashi-bazouk">A Bashi-bazouk</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, painting by <a href="/wiki/Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me" title="Jean-Léon Gérôme">Jean-Léon Gérôme</a>, 1869</div></div></div>
<p>Beginning several centuries ago, during the period of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, tens of thousands of <a href="/wiki/Zanj" title="Zanj">Zanj</a> captives were brought by slave traders to plantations and agricultural areas situated between <a href="/wiki/Antalya_Province" title="Antalya Province">Antalya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Some of their ancestry remained <i>in situ</i>, and many migrated to larger cities and towns. Other black slaves were transported to <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a>, from where they or their descendants later reached the <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a> area through the <a href="/wiki/Population_exchange_between_Greece_and_Turkey" title="Population exchange between Greece and Turkey">population exchange between Greece and Turkey</a> in 1923, or indirectly from <a href="/wiki/Ayval%C4%B1k" title="Ayvalık">Ayvalık</a> in pursuit of work.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_Asia">Southern Asia</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Siddi" title="Siddi">Siddi</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Siddi_Girl.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Siddi_Girl.jpg/170px-Siddi_Girl.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Siddi_Girl.jpg/255px-Siddi_Girl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Siddi_Girl.jpg/340px-Siddi_Girl.jpg 2x" data-file-width="536" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Siddi_Girl.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Siddi girl from the town of <a href="/wiki/Yellapur" class="mw-redirect" title="Yellapur">Yellapur</a> in <a href="/wiki/Uttara_Karnataka" class="mw-redirect" title="Uttara Karnataka">Uttara Karnataka</a> district, Karnataka, India.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Siddi" title="Siddi">Siddi</a> are an ethnic group inhabiting <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> whose members are descendants from the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Shah_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shah-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Makran" title="Makran">Makran</a> strip of the <a href="/wiki/Sindh" title="Sindh">Sindh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balochistan,_Pakistan" title="Balochistan, Pakistan">Balochistan</a> provinces in southwestern <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, these Bantu descendants are known as the Makrani.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> There was a brief "Black Power" movement in Sindh in the 1960s and many Siddi are proud of and celebrate their African ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeastern_Asia">Southeastern Asia</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Negritos" class="mw-redirect" title="Negritos">Negritos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africans_in_Malaysia" title="Africans in Malaysia">Africans in Malaysia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ati_woman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ati_woman.jpg/170px-Ati_woman.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ati_woman.jpg/255px-Ati_woman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ati_woman.jpg/340px-Ati_woman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="567" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ati_woman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ati_people" title="Ati people">Ati</a> woman, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;the <a href="/wiki/Negrito" title="Negrito">Negritos</a> are an indigenous people of Southeast Asia.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Negrito" title="Negrito">Negritos</a> are believed to have been the first inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. Once inhabiting Taiwan,<sup id="cite_ref-Jules_Quartly_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jules_Quartly-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Vietnam,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and various other parts of Asia, they are now confined primarily to Thailand,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> the Malay Archipelago, and the Andaman and Nicobar Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Negrito means "little black people" in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> (negrito is the Spanish diminutive of negro, i.e., "little black person"); it is what the Spaniards called the aborigines that they encountered in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-William_Marsden_1834_4_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-William_Marsden_1834_4-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The term <i>Negrito</i> itself has come under criticism in countries like Malaysia, where it is now interchangeable with the more acceptable <a href="/wiki/Semang" title="Semang">Semang</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hajek_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hajek-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> although this term actually refers to a specific group.
</p><p>Negritos in the Philippines, and Southeast Asia in general, face lots of discrimination. Usually, they are marginalized and live in poverty, unable to find employment that will take them.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Europe">Western Europe</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Portuguese" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Portuguese">Afro-Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_people_in_Ireland" title="Black people in Ireland">Black people in Ireland</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Blacks_in_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Blacks in France">Blacks in France</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyacinthe_Rigaud_-_Jeune_n%C3%A8gre_avec_un_arc_(ca.1697).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Hyacinthe_Rigaud_-_Jeune_n%C3%A8gre_avec_un_arc_%28ca.1697%29.jpg/170px-Hyacinthe_Rigaud_-_Jeune_n%C3%A8gre_avec_un_arc_%28ca.1697%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Hyacinthe_Rigaud_-_Jeune_n%C3%A8gre_avec_un_arc_%28ca.1697%29.jpg/255px-Hyacinthe_Rigaud_-_Jeune_n%C3%A8gre_avec_un_arc_%28ca.1697%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Hyacinthe_Rigaud_-_Jeune_n%C3%A8gre_avec_un_arc_%28ca.1697%29.jpg/340px-Hyacinthe_Rigaud_-_Jeune_n%C3%A8gre_avec_un_arc_%28ca.1697%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1445" data-file-height="1893" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyacinthe_Rigaud_-_Jeune_n%C3%A8gre_avec_un_arc_(ca.1697).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Young Negro with a Bow</i> by <a href="/wiki/Hyacinthe_Rigaud" title="Hyacinthe Rigaud">Hyacinthe Rigaud</a>, ca. 1697.</div></div></div>
<p>While census collection of ethnic background is illegal in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, it is estimated that there are about 2.5&#160;– 5 million black people residing there.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Germans" title="Afro-Germans">Afro-Germans</a></div>
<p>As of 2013, there were approximately 800,000 Afro-Germans (not including those of mixed ethnicity). This number is difficult to estimate because the German census does not use race as a category.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Dutch" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Dutch">Afro-Dutch</a></div>
<p>Afro-Dutch are residents of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> who are of Black African or <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Caribbean">Afro-Caribbean</a> ancestry. They tend to be from the former and present Dutch overseas territories of <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>. The Netherlands also has sizable <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verdean</a> and other African communities.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Spaniard" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Spaniard">Afro-Spaniard</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Concha_Buika2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Concha_Buika2.JPG/220px-Concha_Buika2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Concha_Buika2.JPG/330px-Concha_Buika2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Concha_Buika2.JPG/440px-Concha_Buika2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Concha_Buika2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish singer <a href="/wiki/Concha_Buika" title="Concha Buika">Concha Buika</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The term "<a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>" has been used in Europe in a broader, somewhat derogatory sense to refer to <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Menocal,_María_Rosa_2002_page_241_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Menocal,_María_Rosa_2002_page_241-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> especially those of <a href="/wiki/Arab_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab people">Arab</a> or <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Berber</a> ancestry, whether living in North Africa or Iberia.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Moors were not a distinct or <a href="/wiki/Ethnonym" title="Ethnonym">self-defined</a> people.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Medieval and early modern Europeans applied the name to Muslim Arabs, Berbers, Black Africans and Europeans alike.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a>, writing in the 7th century, claimed that the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word Maurus was derived from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <i>mauron</i>, μαύρον, which is the Greek word for black. Indeed, by the time Isidore of Seville came to write his <i>Etymologies</i>, the word Maurus or "Moor" had become an adjective in Latin, "for the Greeks call black, mauron". "In Isidore's day, Moors were black by definition..."<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Afro-Spaniard" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Spaniard">Afro-Spaniards</a> are <a href="/wiki/Spanish_nationality_law" title="Spanish nationality law">Spanish nationals</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West</a>/<a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central African</a> ancestry. They today mainly come from <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gambia">Gambia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>. Additionally, many Afro-Spaniards born in Spain are from the former Spanish colony <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>. Today, there are an estimated 683,000 Afro-Spaniards in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Black_British" class="mw-redirect" title="Black British">Black British</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mary_Seacole_Drawing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mary_Seacole_Drawing.jpg/170px-Mary_Seacole_Drawing.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mary_Seacole_Drawing.jpg/255px-Mary_Seacole_Drawing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mary_Seacole_Drawing.jpg/340px-Mary_Seacole_Drawing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="527" data-file-height="649" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mary_Seacole_Drawing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A painting of <a href="/wiki/Mary_Seacole" title="Mary Seacole">Mary Seacole</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a>, at the 2001 census there were over a million black people in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>; 1% of the total population described themselves as "Black Caribbean", 0.8% as "Black African", and 0.2% as "Black other".<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Britain encouraged the immigration of workers from the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>; the first symbolic movement was those who came on the ship the <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_Windrush" class="mw-redirect" title="Empire Windrush">Empire Windrush</a></i>. The preferred official <a href="/wiki/Umbrella_term" class="mw-redirect" title="Umbrella term">umbrella term</a> is "black and minority ethnic" (BME), but sometimes the term "black" is used on its own, to express unified opposition to racism, as in the <a href="/wiki/Southall_Black_Sisters" title="Southall Black Sisters">Southall Black Sisters</a>, which started with a mainly <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">British Asian</a> constituency, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Black_Police_Association_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Black Police Association (United Kingdom)">National Black Police Association</a>, which has a membership of "African, African-Caribbean and Asian origin".<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Europe">Eastern Europe</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Russian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Russian">Afro-Russian</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B5._%D0%91%D1%8E%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%90.%D0%9F._%D0%93%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0.jpg" class="image"><img alt=""
